^(CAS\s+)?(\d{2,7}-\d{2}-\d)$
The ISO 8601 standard specifies a date-time format as follows:
YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ss.sssZ
Here, "YYYY" represents the four-digit year, "MM" represents the two-digit month, and "DD" represents the two-digit day. "T" is a separator indicating the start of the time section. "hh" represents the two-digit hour, "mm" represents the two-digit minute, and "ss.sss" represents the seconds and milliseconds. Finally, "Z" represents the time zone offset, which can be in the format "+hh:mm" or "-hh:mm".

The ISO 8601 standard defines a specific format for representing date and time. The format is as follows:
YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ss.sssZ
Where:
- YYYY represents the four-digit year
- MM represents the two-digit month
- DD represents the two-digit day
- T is a separator indicating the start of the time section
- hh represents the two-digit hour in 24-hour format
- mm represents the two-digit minute
- ss represents the two-digit second
- sss represents the fractional part of the second (optional)
- Z represents the time zone offset in the format +hh:mm or

The ISO 8601 standard for date-time format specifies the following format:
YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ss.sssZ
where:
- YYYY represents the four-digit year
- MM represents the two-digit month
- DD represents the two-digit day
- T is a separator indicating the start of the time section
- hh represents the two-digit hour in 24-hour format
- mm represents the two-digit minute
- ss represents the two-digit second
- sss represents the milliseconds (optional)
- Z represents the time zone offset in the format +hh:mm or -hh:mm (optional)
